Food and Rice Market Falling Sharply

Xin Zha

Yesterday, the rice market along the Suzhou Creek was still in a stagnant state. The market opening in the morning did not show any improvement. The buying trend was loosening. Rural traders had no appetite at all. Only 1,000-2,000 shi were traded in small lots. Jiangyin and Kunshan had sufficient rice stocks. The overall market price dropped by 1-2 jiao. Changshu thick japonica rice and Shipu Jiaoli rice, Fengjing and thin japonica rice, and other goods continued to arrive, but urban and rural shops were unusually sluggish. Prices fell by 1 chi across the board. There were few glutinous rice goods, and prices remained unchanged. Yangdu jian (a type of rice) was apparently firm but secretly weak. There was a lack of Yin Yuan rice (a type of rice), and there was no market.

Hu Nan

Yesterday, there were about twenty boats of goods arriving in the Huangpu River. Sales in the city were extremely slow. The declining trend of Suzhou-Changzhou white japonica rice was intensifying, requiring a cut of a small triangle. There was a slight arrival of Southern gang's Qingpu, Chonggu, Tinglin, and Zhujing early and late rice, but the route was stagnant. Prices opened 3-4 jiao lower across the board. Bian Yin Yuan (another type of rice) was not seen. There was a slight improvement in medium-quality transactions. Yangdu jian was affected by foreign rice, and the price fell by 1 chi. Transactions for various goods were around 600-700 dan.

Weak Source Supply Makes it Difficult to Ease Wheat Prices

Yesterday's wheat market showed an initial flatness followed by firmness. Initially, the rising exchange rate of the previous day inevitably stirred the hearts of people inside and outside the industry. However, because the general inland traders are currently in the midst of the new wheat market season, the source of supply in various production areas is still desolate. That is, the combined prices in various places are also higher than those in this port. As a result, the source of supply in this port is weak, and the general middleman has not been enthusiastic. Therefore, although there has been a huge change in the gold price, people's hearts can turn stable. As a result, this month is larger than the previous day's two fen, July is larger one fen, August and September is larger three fen, October and November is larger one fen. The current wheat market is not smooth. Although 3,500 bags of Nanjing and Hezhou and Chuzhou wheat have been opened, there has not been a real transaction. Only the goods of the trading house still have factory matching, and the opened high Chuzhou wheat is 3 taels 9 qian 1 fen, followed by 3 taels 8 qian 7 fen 3 taels 8 qian 5 fen.

Flour Market Initially Falls and Then Rises

Yesterday's flour market, after the opening in the morning, each month was affected by the plummeting gold price. Although people's hearts were once impulsive, the opening price of each month was about one fen lower than the previous day. However, because the factories were watching and not selling, and because the inland gangs were thinking about relying on the weak supply of wheat, they saw an opportunity to absorb it. In addition, the quoted price of foreign wheat continued to be good for about five or six jiao, so the market sentiment in the subsequent trades has stabilized. Until the opening in the afternoon, it was still flat and tired at first. As the wheat market tended to be strong, outsiders covering short positions made the market sentiment in each month slightly hold on. However, if it gradually relaxes, this kind of rejected situation may be difficult to maintain for a long time. As a result, this month is slightly better than the previous day by two li and a half, July is larger one fen, August is larger one fen and a half, September is larger one fen, October and November is larger seven li and a half.

Local News

Various Trade Groups Discussed Amending the Sino-Japanese Agreement Yesterday

Resolved to Form a Research Committee

The proposal was immediately submitted to the committee for research.

In order to maintain the livelihood of industries and businesses involved in Sino-Japanese foreign trade, the China National Products Preservation Association convened a joint meeting yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. Representatives from various industries related to the Sino-Japanese Agreement, national product factories, and trade associations gathered to discuss the Sino-Japanese Agreement. Details of the proceedings are as follows:

Attending Groups

Representatives from the following groups attended yesterday's meeting: Ma Yaoxian from the Danyang Silk Traders Association, Liu Fuqing from the Suzhou Iron and Mechanical Silk Weaving Industry Association, Yu Wenqing and Shi Junqing from the Wuxian Yarn and Satin Industry Association, Ge Tianhao from the National Federation of Commerce, Liu Qianfu and Xin Guozhu from the Shanghai Ramie Cloth Industry Association, Wu Huinong from the Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association, Xu Hanzhang from the Shanghai Porcelain Industry Association, Weng Rongbing from the Central Soap Factory, Fan Zhongqiao from the China Agricultural and Mining Company, Yu Xingben from the Da Zhonghua Rubber Factory, Shao Jinqing from the Zhenhua Paint Factory, Cao Jingyu, Liu Shuming, and Ren Shenting from the Shanghai Seafood Association, Wang Xingyi from the Shanghai Brocade Guild, Wang Jie'an and Wang Hanqiang from the China National Products Preservation Association, and over fifty other individuals.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Wang Jie'an reported, stating that the meeting was convened by the China National Products Preservation Association with the approval of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to discuss amending the Sino-Japanese Agreement, which was signed on May 6, 1930, for a term of three years, expiring on May 5, 1933. To amend the agreement, a proposal must be submitted within six months of its expiration; otherwise, it will remain in effect for another three years. Currently, national products exported to Japan are subject to a 70% tax, while Japanese goods imported into China are subject to an 8% tax. As a result, national products cannot be sold abroad smoothly, while foreign goods can be imported into China in large quantities. This is obviously unequal and requires amendment. He requested that the attending representatives express their opinions as much as possible and work together to find solutions, hoping that they would conduct careful research to propose suggestions for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to adopt.

Proposed Cases

The Brocade Guild proposed: (1) Japanese silk transported to Korea is taxed at 8%, while Chinese silk is taxed at 70%, which is a vast disparity. Article 2 of the agreement states that the tax rate on imported goods should be the same as that on domestic goods. Therefore, Chinese silk transported to Korea should be taxed at the same rate as Japanese silk, which is 8%, to ensure equality and conform to the original text of the agreement. This is what should be strongly advocated for when the agreement expires. (2) Korea was originally our affiliated state, but Japanese interference in its internal affairs led to the Sino-Japanese War of 1894. Unfortunately, we were defeated, and Korea was forcibly annexed by Japan. Although this was due to might, justice was not served. Now that the Treaty of Shimonoseki has long expired, the territory of Korea should have been recovered and should not remain under Japanese control for long. Korea was the fiefdom of Jizi of Yin and Shang and should be within the Chinese territory. How can we allow it to be oppressed by other ethnic groups for so long and be subjected to the discrimination of this unequal tax rate? We should request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to lodge a protest to achieve the goal of recovery. (3) The tax rates for trade between the two countries should be equal. If Chinese silk transported to Korea can be subject to the same tax rate as Japanese silk when the agreement is amended, this would be a satisfactory solution. Otherwise, the customs duty on Japanese silk imported into China should be increased to 70% to serve as a countermeasure. The Ramie Cloth Guild also proposed demanding that the import and export tax rates between China and Japan be equal.

Resolutions

It was resolved to form a committee to study the Sino-Japanese Agreement. The structure is as follows: (1) It shall be named the Sino-Japanese Agreement Tariff Research Committee. (2) The committee shall consist of seventeen members. (3) Three standing committee members shall be elected from among the committee members. (4) Each committee member should be nominated by the relevant organization. (5) Nominations are sought for one member from the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, one member from the Wuxian Chamber of Commerce, two members from the Shanghai Ramie Cloth Guild, one member from the Shanghai Machine-Made National Products Factory Federation, one member from the National General Chamber of Commerce, one member from the Shanghai Porcelain Industry Association, two members from the Shanghai Seafood Association, one member from the Shanghai Citizens' National Products Promotion Association, three members from the Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association, one member from the Shanghai Embroidery Industry Association, one member from the China National Products Preservation Association, one member from the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Federation, and one member from the National Products Factory Federation. (6) Committee members should be nominated by various organizations within one week. After all members have been nominated, the committee will be convened. (7) The China National Products Preservation Association is designated as the convener. (8) The address of the meeting will be temporarily located within the Preservation Association at Nine Acres. The proposed cases will be submitted for research after the research committee is established.

Anti-Drug Association Asks Authorities to Pay Attention to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Instructions

The China National Anti-Drug Association stated that the authorities' approach to banning opium has adopted a policy of "prohibition through taxation," collecting opium taxes and allowing sales. Although the Ministry of Finance has denied being in charge of this matter, its content clearly violates the opium prohibition regulations and international treaties. Public appeals and public opinion are in an uproar, and local party departments and anti-drug groups have sent numerous letters and telegrams expressing their opposition, but without any effect. Yesterday, the full text of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug instructions was specially published, hoping to serve as a guide for opium prohibition and to draw the attention of the authorities.

Shanghai to Establish a General Opium Suppression and Investigation Office

According to a certain gentleman in the anti-opium circles, the central government has decided to establish a special office for opium suppression. A General Opium Suppression and Investigation Office will be established in Shanghai, and Opium Suppression and Investigation Offices will be established in provinces such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei. Not only will the planting and smoking of opium be prohibited, but also investigation sub-offices will be established in major coastal, riverine, and land-sea intersection ports to prevent the trafficking of opium and similar drugs. The methods will be handled in accordance with the recently promulgated Opium Suppression Law. In the future, opium cases will be handled by this office and will no longer be transferred from local administrative organs. Local garrisoned armies or land and water public security police teams must not overstep their authority to interfere, so as to unify power. It is reported that Jiangsu Province has already started the process of organizing its office. It is heard that Li Muqing has been appointed to prepare for the Shanghai general office, and it will be established soon.

Shanghai City Opium Suppression and Investigation Sub-Office Director Feng Wenyu, upon receiving the order from the General Office, is actively organizing the sub-office for official business. Director Feng has selected No. 81 Manufacturing Bureau Road in the Southern City as the sub-office address. It was officially established yesterday and started operating. Notices have been sent to all military, police, and political organs in the city.

Comrade Tao Yishan of the Shanghai County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee was ordered by the Provincial Reorganization Committee in September of the 19th year [1930] to serve as a member of the County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee and was also designated as the Director of the Organization Department. To Minister Kong Jun of the Nanjing Ministry of Industry: Regarding the reorganization of the former Wusong Chamber of Commerce into the Wusong Branch Office of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, this Bureau previously submitted it to the Municipal Government, which forwarded it to your Ministry for approval and reply, agreeing to proceed as proposed, and the order has been forwarded for notification. However, two months after the former Wusong Chamber of Commerce moved, it has not yet complied with the order and continues to use the name of the Baoshan County Wusong Chamber of Commerce within this city. Former Chairman Zheng Shushan has also been accused of colluding with tax agencies to extort shipowners and collect membership fees. If this deliberate defiance of laws and regulations is not strictly corrected, it will not only disrupt the organizational system of the Chamber of Commerce in this city but also conflict with the Central Government's previous aim of dispatching personnel to reorganize merchant groups and strive for unity. Currently, on the 20th of this month, this Bureau, together with the Public Security Bureau and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, sent personnel to the former Chamber of Commerce to receive the documents and other items. In addition to ordering the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to organize a branch office within a time limit and be responsible for the liquidation, this report is being sent to your office for review and approval for record-keeping. respectfully, Pan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs. (Stamped)

Submitted to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Yesterday, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs issued an order to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce regarding the reorganization of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce into a branch office: To be complied with. This bureau has already ordered the said chamber to send personnel on the 20th of this month to accompany personnel dispatched by this bureau and the Public Security Bureau to take over the assets of the former Wusong Chamber of Commerce. Party Headquarters' Letter to Merchants and Citizens

The Eighth District Party Headquarters' letter to the merchants and citizens of Wusong regarding the reorganization of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce states: Fellow merchants and citizens of Wusong, Wusong is a prosperous commercial district, and according to the regulations of the Chamber of Commerce Law, it is entitled to either establish a separate chamber of commerce or a branch office. However, it is not absolutely necessary to establish a separate chamber of commerce. The Bureau of Social Affairs and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, in order to safeguard and enhance commercial interests while maintaining unified organization, prudently suggested that establishing a branch office is more appropriate. In particular, it is not disregarding the Chamber of Commerce Law. Some people among the merchants and citizens of Wusong mistakenly believe that this reorganization is suppressing the merchants and citizens, which is a misunderstanding of the Chamber of Commerce Law. The sole responsibility of the former reorganization committee is to unify and reorganize merchant groups. It is unreasonable for a few merchants and citizens of Wusong to criticize it as a pretext and oppose the reorganization. Furthermore, advocating for the preservation of the old Wusong Chamber of Commerce organization is even less justified. We must understand that changing the Wusong Chamber of Commerce into a branch office is merely a change in organization and a change in name. The group is still a popular organization of the merchants and citizens of Wusong. Since the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is carefully selecting candidates for the director of the branch office, the merchants and citizens of Wusong need not worry too much. If this reorganization is seen as disallowing the existence of the Chamber of Commerce, and opposing the reorganization is regarded as "fighting for survival," such a view is too naive and laughable. In the Ministry of Industry's instructions to the Chamber, there are indeed a few words saying, "Upon learning, after investigating the various points mentioned by the Chamber, there is some justification. Wait for a factual report to be submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and then instruct compliance." However, we must also understand that the Municipal Government's approval of the Ministry of Industry's consultation states that it is appropriate to change the Wusong Chamber of Commerce into a branch office, and the reasons are sufficient. It should be approved as proposed and instructed to be notified. We should pay more attention to this. Moreover, the Ministry of Industry's instructions to the Chamber only said, "Wait for a factual report to be submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and then instruct compliance." It did not say that Wusong must establish a separate chamber of commerce, nor did it say that Wusong will definitely be allowed to establish a separate chamber of commerce in the future. We hope that the merchants of Wusong will carefully study this point. As for the debts of the former Wusong Chamber of Commerce, the responsible personnel of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce have also clearly stated that after the Municipal Chamber of Commerce reviews and deems them legitimate, the Chamber of Commerce will be responsible for reorganizing and repaying them. The merchants and citizens should not use this as an excuse to oppose the reorganization. It must be understood that at this time of rampant bandits and intense military situations at the front, the people of the whole country should be united in heart and mind to maintain local peace, so that our central government can concentrate its efforts and focus on the work of suppressing bandits. If we act rashly without careful consideration and allow a few troublemakers to incite and instigate, hoping to use the former responsible personnel of the Chamber of Commerce as their puppets and tools to disrupt order, causing various illegal actions such as automatic shutdowns, to achieve their destructive ambitions, it will not only violate the government's grand vision of eliminating bandits and actively building, but also betray the original intention of the merchants of Wusong to maintain the community. Fellow merchants and citizens of Wusong, we can formally contribute our opinions to the government, but our misunderstandings must submit to the correction of the authorities. We should represent the real people and make legitimate and legal demands. We must not be deceived, incited, or used to commit illegal actions. We love the merchants of Wusong, we love the merchant community of Wusong, and we especially hope that the merchants and citizens of Wusong can have a legitimate and legal organization. The Executive Committee of the Eighth District of the Chinese Nationalist Party in Shanghai Special City, June 23, 1931.

Ministry of Railways Cancels Proposal to Abolish the Transportation Industry

But 5% Commission Will No Longer Be Paid

Previously, due to the Ministry of Railways' proposed abolition of the transportation industry, the local transportation industry convened a meeting of all members to discuss countermeasures and sent representatives to the Ministry of Railways to explain their difficulties. It is now learned that the Ministry of Railways has determined that the industry has performed well in circulating goods and assisting transportation, and has a long history. Therefore, the proposal to abolish the industry will not be implemented. However, the 5% commission (i.e., 5 cents per dollar) paid to the industry at the end of each year will be abolished from now on and will no longer be paid.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Resolves Merger of Transportation Organizations

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has repeatedly received instructions from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, stating that the business nature of the members of the Transportation Industry Association and the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Transfer Industry Association is completely the same. According to the regulations that no two industry associations of the same nature can exist in the same area, they should be merged immediately. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened several discussions, but no agreement was reached due to differing opinions. Yesterday, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened another mediation session. Representatives from the Transportation Industry Association, Li Mulian and Wang Xufu, and representatives from the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Transfer Industry Association, Shen Huiquan and Ge Laichi, attended. Sun Mingqi, representing the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, explained the purpose of the meeting and repeatedly stated the advantages and disadvantages. After soliciting the consent of both parties, the following decisions were made: (1) The headquarters will be established in a central location, and the original headquarters of both parties will be converted into branch offices in the north and south; (2) Both parties will appoint members of a merger preparatory committee to handle all merger matters. It is reported that the Chamber of Commerce has sent the decision to the respective associations, urging them to strictly comply, and has submitted the decision to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs for record.

Uniform Weights and Measures

All Kinds of Equipment Needed by Various Industries

Will Be Collected and Distributed by the Association

The implementation of the new system of weights and measures in this city is scheduled for July 1 as the uniform deadline. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has repeatedly ordered the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to notify all industry associations to comply. With the uniform deadline approaching, the bureau has specially ordered the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and various industry associations to assist in the implementation so that it can be completed on time. All new equipment required by various industries, whether members or non-members, will be reported to the Municipal Weights and Measures Inspection Institute by the respective industry associations, and pre-ordered from the weights and measures manufacturing factory for unified collection and distribution. The quantity and types of equipment to be requisitioned by each business will be determined by the business itself. The industry associations must sell the equipment at the original fixed price and must not raise the price. It is reported that the Weights and Measures Inspection Institute and the manufacturing factory are both located at the original site of the Flower Tree Industry Association on Xieqiao Manufacturing Bureau Road. Recently, vendors and various industries have been crowding the place to requisition new equipment.

Ministry of Industry Implements Tea Inspection

To Eliminate Malpractices and Enhance International Credit

Yesterday, the Ministry of Industry instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: Regarding the matter of instructions, tea has always been a major export of our country, but in recent years, sales have declined, and there is a trend of collapse. The reason for this is that although teas from Japan, India, Ceylon, and other countries have emerged to compete, the main reason is that the manufacturing of Chinese tea adheres to the old rules, does not seek improvement, and is mixed with impurities and counterfeits, which is a major cause of the decline in foreign trade. In order to eliminate the malpractices of the tea industry, urge improvement, and enhance international trade credit, the Ministry has decided to implement inspection, which can no longer be delayed. The Regulations for Tea Inspection have been formulated and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing, and have been promulgated by the Ministry. In addition to ordering the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry to comply with the regulations and implement the inspection, a copy is sent for your information and to be forwarded to the tea industry organizations for information. This order.

Business License for Brokers Temporarily Handled by the County

Municipal Bureau of Finance Responds to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Yesterday, the Business Tax Preparatory Office of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance responded to a letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which stated that the Charcoal Industry Association of this city stated in a letter that the broker's licenses have always been issued by the county. Now that they are called business licenses, it seems redundant if they are still issued by the county. The letter requested that a method be determined for forwarding them. Upon approval, the broker's license tax is used to fund education expenses in Jiangsu Province, according to the provincial and municipal division of powers. It is temporarily collected by the county bureau. Although the name of the broker's license has been changed to business tax in Jiangsu Province, it seems that the tax should still be handled by the county bureau in this city before it is recovered, in order to avoid disputes. The request in the letter is approved. A corresponding letter is returned.

Minutes of the Meeting of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's National Products Shopping Mall

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce's Commodity Exhibition Hall National Products Shopping Mall convened its second committee meeting the day before yesterday. Ye Huijun, Luo Qinghua, Zheng Chengqing, Ye Xiaoshan, Xi Guansheng, Fang Jiange, Pan Dechun, Ding Xunhao, Wang Lisun, Pei Weimin, Ye Youcai, Zhang Baoshan, and Xu Dianhuang were present. The chairman was Ye Xiaoshan. The resolutions are as follows: (1) The Manufacturers' Representatives Conference resolved to hire members of the Commodity Price Evaluation Committee and decided on the number of members. It was resolved that the number of members be fixed at 15, and the following organizations be invited to each appoint one person: Chinese National Products Maintenance Association, Municipal Citizens' National Products Promotion Association, National Products Factory Federation, Mechanized National Products Factory Federation, Women's National Products Promotion Association, Municipal Chamber of Commerce National Products Promotion Committee, Electrical Industry Association, Silk and Satin Industry Association, Knitting Industry Association, Cosmetics Industry Association, Straw Hat Industry Association, Copper and Tin Industry Association, Department Store Industry Association, Mercerized Cotton Weaving Industry Association, Biscuit Candy and Canned Food Industry Association, etc. (2) The Manufacturers' Representatives Conference resolved to request the provision of bicycle delivery vehicles. It was resolved that the vehicles and delivery workers will be prepared by the shopping mall office. (3) The Manufacturers' Representatives Conference resolved to request a reconsideration of the electric fan expenses. It was resolved that a total of 16 electric fans will be installed in the hall, and the electricity bill will be borne by the shopping mall. (4) Should salespersons of each factory be required to copy the price of each item sold clearly on a separate sales slip for the purpose of checking diligence and laziness and giving rewards at the end of the year? It was resolved that the shopping mall will provide suggestions on the methods for rewarding employees to each factory, and each factory will adopt them on its own. (5) How should failure to issue invoices and haggling be punished? It was resolved that each factory should require salespersons to issue invoices for all sales above one dime. Those who fail to issue invoices once will be warned first. Those who fail three times will be notified to the factory to dismiss the salesperson. If haggling is discovered, the shopping mall will impose a fine of ten times the amount. (6) In addition to placing advertisements in Shen Bao and Xin Bao and film advertisements, should street parade advertisements and other promotional methods be added this month? It was resolved that street parade advertisements will continue for another 16 days until July 5. (7) Should each factory set up a counter supervisor to supervise the business situation of the counter and guide the salespersons at any time? It was resolved that each factory will be notified to set up one counter supervisor and report the name to the shopping mall office so that the supervisor can be contacted in case of any issues. Furthermore, salespersons must wear badges, and factories must not occupy the aisles with goods. Those who do not comply with the rules will have their goods confiscated.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The Ninety-Third Time

The Ninety-Third Inspection Report of the Central Bank's Issuance Reserve states: This council is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of convertible notes of this bank in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations. The 93rd inspection was held in the Issuance Bureau of this bank on June 20, 1931. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: A. The total amount of convertible notes issued is 33,725,308 silver dollars, including: silver dollar notes of 31,700,920 yuan, subsidiary coin notes of 2,016,088 yuan. The total amount of convertible note reserve fund is 33,725,308 yuan, including: cash reserve of silver dollars of 23,827,887.20 yuan. The cash reserve includes 16,470,826.45 yuan stored in the issuance treasury of this bank, 2,310,190 yuan stored in branch banks in various ports, 5,046,870.075 yuan stored in fellow banks, and a guarantee reserve equivalent to 9,897,420.08 yuan in silver dollars. B. The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 1,000,000 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserve fund is 1,000,000 yuan. The reserve fund includes 400,000 US dollars, stored in a local fellow bank, at a fixed price of 40% customs gold as above. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the amount of cash exceeds 60% and the amount of guarantee is less than 40%, which is in line with the regulations. This report is hereby made. June 20, 1931, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilong.

Fellow villagers of Songjiang petition to retain County Magistrate Jin

Jin Qingzhang, the magistrate of Songjiang County, has served for three years and his political achievements are evident. Fellow villagers in Shanghai, Qian Gongpu, Zhu Pengling, Huo Yuanjin, Chen Ding, Shen Xun, Wang Longwen, and over thirty others, convened a meeting to telegraph the superiors to retain him. The telegram reads: "To the Director of the Civil Affairs Department: It was recently heard that County Magistrate Jin Qingzhang of our county is to be transferred to the province for appointment. The news has caused great alarm. County Magistrate Jin has served for three years, and has been meticulous in strictly prohibiting opium and gambling, suppressing bandits, and rectifying academic morals. His virtuous policies have been widely embraced, and all families admire him. This sudden transfer is a disappointment to the public. Although talents like Shiyuan (referring to Pang Tong, a famous strategist) may not be suitable for governing a small territory, we, Gongpu and others, were born in Songjiang and cannot bear to remain silent and allow a virtuous official to leave. In addition to telegraphing the Ministry of Interior, we dare to telegraph your office, hoping that you will consider the local situation and withdraw the order, so as to fulfill the wishes of the people and comfort public sentiment. We would be deeply grateful."

Lost children records

各工会消息

Various labor union news

The Fresh Pork Industry Workers' Union submitted a document to the Municipal Party Department yesterday, stating that a worker was beaten by a crowd and the case was reported to the police post, which transferred it to the court for investigation. The document detailed the circumstances and requested the association to review the case, uphold justice, and provide practical relief. It stated that there have been instances of forced purchases in the fresh pork industry market, which have been reported to the authorities for investigation. Unexpectedly, at around 1:00 PM on June 23, at the Xuejiabang Fresh Pork Market, just as the market was opening, a butcher from the Changyuan Pig Farm wanted to buy a pig at the lowest price. At that time, the pig buyer Lin Ziwen was unwilling to sell cheaply because it involved his capital. The butcher tried to take it by force, and a dispute arose. Liang Anmin, a runner from Changyuan, mediated. Suddenly, another butcher, Zhang Xiaogen, relied on his strength to help and abuse, and became angry with Liang, thinking that he was preventing the customer from selling. He shouted and gathered a crowd to surround and beat Liang, punching and kicking him, and pressing him to the ground, making him unable to move, almost killing him. The butcher, knowing that he had caused trouble and that it involved human life, forcibly took someone else's scissors and stabbed his own leg, in order to shift the blame. This was witnessed by Xu Hongfu and others. His sinister intentions were unexpected. Fortunately, the police post detained both parties and transferred them to the court for review. Naturally, they will quietly await legal sanctions. Under such circumstances, the lives of all the pork industry workers serving in the market are in danger. Therefore, public anger is overwhelming, and they advocate a general strike to avoid the danger. After the representatives of the trade association tried their best to dissuade them, the workers unanimously decided to wait for three days. If there is no fair solution and no adequate protection, a labor strike may occur, which will affect more than a thousand meat shops and hundreds of pig buyers, putting them in a state of suspension. Therefore, they are making an urgent appeal, hoping that your association will review the case and promptly forward it to the court for a fair ruling, in order to appease public anger and ensure safety. This would be a great kindness.

Local News Two

离奇夺子案

Bizarre child abduction case

Zhang Qinchu nearly loses his beloved son

Fortunately, the child has six toes on his left foot

Zhang Qinchu, a local resident, is 32 years old and works as a clerk at the Xiangmao Soap Company on the Bund. He has lived at No. 6 Daqing Lane, Old West Gate, for more than six years. Zhang married Ms. Wu, who is the same age as Zhang and a native of Zhejiang. They have been married for ten years and have a son and a daughter. The eldest daughter, named Aide, is eight years old, and the son, named Rongguang, is four years old. Zhang's family of several people enjoy a happy family life. Unexpectedly, yesterday at around 11:00 AM, a northerner dressed in a Zhongshan suit claiming to be Wu Maoting and a woman from Jiangbei, along with several police officers from the Second District General Office, first knocked frequently on Zhang's back door. At that time, Zhang's brother-in-law, Wu Shuiting, opened the door. The police immediately asked if this was a knitted socks factory. Wu replied that this was where the clerk of the Xiangmao Soap Company lived and there was no so-called socks factory. After the police finished questioning, they repeatedly asked the residents at the entrance of the lane. Finally, they returned to Zhang's house. At that time, Zhang's young son, Rongguang, was playing in the living room. The woman from Jiangbei stared at Rongguang for a long time and said that he looked very much like her son. After saying that, the person in the Zhongshan suit instructed the police to detain Rongguang, Zhang's brother-in-law Wu Shuiting, and Zhang's sister-in-law Wu Yuwen together. After the district chief questioned them in detail, the person in the Zhongshan suit claimed to be Wu Maoting, who had held military positions. He stated that he and his wife had a son in Shanghai in 1929. At that time, he had to leave Shanghai for work, so he took his wife along. Because it was difficult to carry the baby along the way, he entrusted Qiao Shen, a woman from Gaoyou whom he knew and lived in Gaochang Temple, to take care of him and paid her 8 yuan a month for breastfeeding. At first, they often exchanged letters, but eventually there was no news. When he returned to Shanghai this time, he visited Shen, but she had disappeared without a trace. Yesterday morning, he happened to meet Shen near the World on Aidaoya Road. When he questioned her, Shen claimed that the child had been sold by her to someone for a price of 30 yuan. However, Shen said that she still remembered the address of the person who took care of him as being in a residence in Daqing Lane, Old West Gate. Therefore, she was detained and the police were sent to investigate at the address. However, after inquiring with the residents in the lane, there was no such child. Later, they went to Zhang's house and saw a child who was about the same age as her son. It was generally determined that Shen had sold him to the Zhang family. When asked Qiao Shen, she confessed that she had initially taken care of the child entrusted to her. However, eventually, even though she was paid 8 yuan a month, she did not receive any money after a while, so she was unable to continue taking care of him. Therefore, she entrusted a barber whom she knew, who then entrusted a Zhang to sell him to a resident in Daqing Lane, receiving 30 yuan. When asked Wu Yuwen and Wu Shuiting, they both claimed that he was their sister's biological son. It was absurd for someone to come and falsely claim him now. After questioning, the order was given to temporarily detain Wu Yuwen and Rongguang. Wu Shuiting rushed to the Xiangmao Foreign Company on the Bund and told Zhang Qinchu in detail. Zhang was furious when he heard this and rushed to the Second District General Office, declaring that he was his biological son. District Chief Wang reviewed the case again. Both sides still insisted on their own words. Zhang had no choice but to ask if there were any special marks on the child's body or any special differences in his feet. Shen and the person in the Zhongshan suit both said that he was no different from ordinary people. Zhang then took off the leather shoes that Rongguang was wearing on his left foot in front of everyone. Everyone watched closely. Unexpectedly, next to the smallest toe on Rongguang's left foot, there was another toe. It was clearly a six-toed child. Shen and the others were speechless. Thus, this bizarre child abduction case was revealed.

赵案凶犯讯结

The Zhao case murderers are interrogated

Verdict to be announced soon

The murderers Xia Shaoen, Wang Jinshan, and Cheng Enbo, who assassinated Zhao Tieqiao, the general manager of the China Merchants Bureau, have been prosecuted by the local court. Judge Zhao Yongzhou has been investigating the case for several months and has finally come to a clear understanding. Yesterday morning, the three murderers were brought to the case for interrogation and still denied their crimes. However, the murderers had already confessed to the prosecutor. The judge then announced the start of the debate. The prosecutor argued that the defendants had committed the crime of murder and requested a public trial. After the appointed defense lawyer defended them, the judge announced the end of the debate and waited for the verdict. The defendants were sent back to prison.

朱元桃案蒸骨后再鉴定

Zhu Yuantao case: bones steamed and re-identified

The cause of death of Zhu Yuantao, a native of Lianshui County, Jiangsu Province, is unknown. The case was accused of murdering her own husband. After the coffin was opened and the bones were steamed for examination, both parties were dissatisfied. The case was submitted to the High Court for review. All the bones were packed in a wooden box and sent to the High Court. In order to avoid injustice, the High Court ordered the Shanghai Local Court to send the bones to the hospital for identification. Yesterday, bailiff Zhu Wan-yuan went to Jiangsu and took the bone box to the Shanghai Court, waiting to be sent to the hospital for identification.

朱礼耕案两绑匪处死刑

Zhu Ligeng case: two kidnappers sentenced to death

Zhang and Hao were both sentenced to death

Zhang Shenshi sentenced to two years and six months

Hao Soshi transferred to the French Court

Zhu Ligeng, the owner of the Zhongfu Silk Mill in Chabei, who lived on Changsha Road, was kidnapped at 8:30 AM on April 4 when he went to the factory to work. Fortunately, Zhu was alert and escaped. Later, the French police arrested the kidnappers Zhang Debiao, Hao Zifeng, and their wives Zhang Shenshi and Hao Soshi. They were transferred to the Special District Local Court. After repeated trials, it was confirmed that they carried a pistol for the bandits to use. Only Hao Soshi had not participated. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi took the bench and ordered Zhang et al. to be brought forward and sentenced. Zhang and Hao were sentenced to death for jointly kidnapping for ransom in accordance with the regulations on punishing kidnappers. Zhang Shenshi was sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment for intending to provide others with the means to commit a crime and possessing military firearms. The number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed was allowed to offset the imprisonment by two days for one day. Hao Soshi was acquitted. After the verdict, police lawyer Wang Yaotang stood up and stated that the police had no objection to the acquittal of Hao Soshi, but since she had been sentenced to one year of imprisonment by the French court in another case after being arrested by the French police, although she was acquitted in this case, she must be sent back to the French Concession for execution and could not be released. Judge Wu then ordered Hao Soshi to be returned to the French court for imprisonment. The remaining three male and female bandits were still held separately pending confirmation before being executed according to the verdict.

United in Death

A Mechanic Foreman Makes a Trap for Himself

How Deep is the Young Woman's Affection?

Zhang Panqin from Pudong was a foreman mechanic at the Zhonghua Arts and Crafts Society in Caojiadu. He moved his family from Pudong to No. 71, Cunshan Lane, Caojiadu, to be closer to work and avoid the tiring commute. A young woman in the same building, whose husband was away working in another place, felt lonely in the unfamiliar alleyways and had an affair with Zhang. Despite frequent verbal abuse from Zhang's wife, her passionate love did not diminish. Zhang's wife forced Zhang to move to No. 95, Xinkang Lane, to avoid the woman, but the young woman also moved to be near him, almost like devoted lovers. Zhang began to feel the pain of his self-made trap. Recently, pressured by economic hardship, quarrels increased when his money ran out, and he had the idea of suicide. On the night before last at 7 PM, he and the young woman went to the Andong Inn on Hubei Road and rented room 318, using the alias Zhang Fangzhen, age 26. After the waiter left, Zhang immediately closed the door tightly and wrote several suicide notes, sending them to family and friends. Then, he took out the prepared opium paste and swallowed it with the young woman, and they lay neck to neck to sleep, waiting for death to come and achieve their goal of dying together. After someone noticed, they quickly reported it to the Laozha police, who sent them to the hospital. However, Zhang's poison had already entered his internal organs, and he was beyond cure. He died. The young woman had taken less poison than Zhang, and her life could probably be saved. Zhang's body was taken by the police to the Forensic Examination Office on Faelon Road that night. Yesterday morning, Judge Guo of the Special District Local Court went to the office to confirm the cause of death. Zhang's younger brother, Zhang Yushu, explained the reasons for his brother's suicide. Judge Guo ordered Zhang Yushu to sign a guarantee and take the body for burial.

Gu Ronggen Suddenly Has a Wife Appearing After His Death

Gu Did Not Marry Before His Death

Problems Arising from Assets

Gu Daquan from Wuxi passed away many years ago. His eldest son, Peitang, and third son, Rongjin, also followed him to the grave early. Only the second son, Rongzeng, and the youngest son, Ronggen, remained. Rongzeng had a son, Zhenhua, who is now nineteen years old and graduated from Fudan University and is now able to be independent. However, Ronggen, although he was a comprador for the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha’s Fengyang Maru ship, had assets of forty to fifty thousand taels of silver, he was still a widower. However, he suddenly suffered a stroke and died suddenly on February 5th of this year. The Gu family, believing that they could not allow the deceased to become a neglected spirit, decided through public discussion that Zhenhua would inherit the lineage. Therefore, on March 14th, an inheritance agreement was written and signed by the public witnesses Huang Gu, Yue Tingyuan, Deng Shucai, Huang Yiren, and Lu Xueling. Recently, a woman from Suzhou, Xu Ruizhi, stepped forward, claiming to be the legal wife of the deceased Gu Ronggen. Although she had no children, her husband had an affair with a woman surnamed Mou, who gave birth to a son named Genghua, who should inherit his father's rights. Why was it necessary to establish someone else's son as an heir? Upon hearing her words, Gu's relatives were incredulous. Gu Zhenhua, feeling personally threatened, accused Xu of fabricating facts to covet the inheritance and sued her in the Special District Local Court, requesting confirmation that he was the legal heir of Gu Ronggen. However, Xu also filed a lawsuit against Gu Rongzeng, Zhenhua's biological father. Her purpose was to confirm that she was the guardian of Gu Genghua and to be allowed to manage all of Gu Ronggen's assets. Each side held their own views, and the truth was currently unclear. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Daren opened the court and summoned Xu's lawsuit against Gu for trial. According to the plaintiff Xu Ruizhi's testimony, she married Ronggen in 1915. When they married, Wang Mengnan, Dong Zhichu, Zhu Boyong, Wang Runsen, Tan Kuixian, and other relatives and friends were present to witness the ceremony. The defendant Gu Rongzeng testified that Xu was not his brother's legal wife but only had a concubine relationship. She was originally a divorced concubine of a Li family and only became acquainted with his brother in 1920, living together at No. 872 1/2, Hongxing Lane, Beijing Road. Now she claimed to have formally married his brother, but why did no one in the clan acknowledge it? This was a fabrication of facts. Wang, Dong, Zhu, and other witnesses were brought to court to testify. They all said that although they knew that Xu was Ronggen's woman, they did not witness their marriage. However, Wang Runsen testified that he was the matchmaker for Xu and Gu's marriage. Finally, the defendant's lawyers, Yan Yinwu and Zhang Ding, presented the inheritance document, which stated that Gu Ronggen was unmarried and had no children, proving that the deceased was indeed unmarried. Judge Xie stated that further investigation was needed and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Kidnapping Case Cracked at the Gu Family Residence in Baoshan; Trial Began Yesterday

The Kidnappers are Inhuman

The Female Victims Were Violated One After Another

The Baoshan County Guard Corps cracked a kidnapping pirate ship in Tangqiao, capturing three kidnappers on the spot and rescuing one male hostage and two female hostages from the ship's cabin. They were sent to the Baoshan County Government for trial. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that yesterday (the 23rd) at 9 AM, the trial began under the presiding judge Huang Jie. (1) According to the kidnapper

Yan Zhiqin, also Known as Yan A Si, Testified

He was twenty-nine years old, from Yancheng, and lived in Tanzhiwan, Zhabei, Shanghai. His occupation was rickshaw puller, and he also engaged in kidnapping. His accomplices included Zhou Ermazi, A Da, Tang Youfa, A Er, Xue Renjie, Gao Laoda, Xue Er, Xue San, Jiang Acai, Liu Xiao Erzi (also known as Dao Ai), Tang A San, Yan Zhiqin, Qu San, Gao Laoye, and others, totaling fourteen people. They went to Kunshan to kidnap. That day, they gathered at the Daxiao Ziminzhong in Xiaoshadu, West Shanghai. They were already waiting for me in the Tiger Stove at Chadaijiao. Because I didn't go, they came to my house to find me, and we went to Kunshan together, bringing two long guns, two medium guns, and seven handguns. When we went to kidnap, because I didn't know how to use guns, I went forward empty-handed. First, we kidnapped two women, then a man. Later, they kidnapped an old man, who was ransomed for two thousand yuan. I received one hundred and sixty yuan. This money was with Gao Laoye. Gao said that it would be distributed together after all the hostages were ransomed. I stayed on the boat for five days. Because I felt lonely, I slept with one of the older female hostages and had intercourse with her one night. How much money was needed to ransom these hostages had not yet been decided. Xue Renjie, Gao Laoye, and Zhou Ermazi were the leaders of the gang. I don't know where they live in Shanghai. (2) Kidnapper

Tang Shaolian Testified

He was thirty-one years old, from Yancheng, and lived in Tanzhiwan, Shanghai. His occupation was road worker. The place where I lived was half a mile away from Xue Renjie’s place. Xue Er, Xue San, A Da, A Er, etc., were sworn brothers. On the day we set off, we agreed to meet at the Tiger Stove in Tanzhiwan, Chadaijiao. Then, on the seventh day of the fourth lunar month, we set off from Shanghai and arrived in Kunshan on the ninth, when we began to kidnap. We kidnapped two men and two women, in two separate operations. First, we went to one house and kidnapped two women. Then, we went next door and kidnapped a man. Then, we went to the left and kidnapped another man. After the kidnapping, they were all confined in the boat's cabin. One of the male hostages was later ransomed for two thousand yuan. In reality, there were only one thousand five hundred and fifty yuan. I only received three yuan, given by Xue Renjie. There was still a male hostage, for whom we wanted five hundred yuan. For the two female hostages, we wanted one thousand yuan each, totaling two thousand yuan. None of this had been agreed upon. I had intercourse with the older female hostage for three nights. The younger female hostage was violated by Liu Aidao. There were fourteen people in our gang. Xue Renjie sent me and Yan Zhiqin, Tang Shaolian, to guard the hostages on the boat. Because no one came to ransom the hostages, it has been a month since the kidnapping. My companions have all returned to Shanghai. In Chadaijiao, I heard that Zhou Ermazi, A Da, A Er, A Xiang, and A Si were all arrested. I used to be a road worker. Later, Xue Renjie said to me that being a road worker was very hard. "I'll recommend something to you that can make you rich." I only did kidnapping for the first time. (3) Kidnapper

Liu Daoai Testified

He was twenty-seven years old, from Yancheng, and lived in a thatched shed behind the Fuxing Flour Mill in Xiaoshadu, Shanghai. His occupation was rickshaw puller. Xue Renjie was my uncle. He told me to sleep on the boat. There were fourteen people in our gang. On the third day of the fourth lunar month, my uncle told me to help him and gave me one yuan a day. I watched the hostages, a total of three people, two women and one man. Another male hostage had already been ransomed for one thousand two hundred and fifty yuan. I slept with the older female hostage once and with the younger female hostage twice. Last year, in Yingziwei Township, near Taihu Lake in Suzhou, we kidnapped three men and one woman. After the kidnapping, we hid them in the west end of Caojiadu. The three men paid a total of two thousand five hundred yuan to be ransomed. The female hostage was not raped. (4) Female Hostage

Xu Wu Shi Testified

She was thirty-three years old, from Kunshan, and lived in Zhangpu. Her husband's name was Xu Liukui. On the ninth night of the fourth lunar month, I was kidnapped from my mother's house. There were only my mother and daughter at home. My uncle next door, Wu Yunzhou, had already gone back. After kidnapping me first, they poled the boat over to kidnap Wu Yunzhou. After the kidnapping, my uncle was ransomed for one thousand two hundred and fifty yuan. Including today, it has only been six days. When they were ransomed, they were sent to Shanghai on a Trapa natans boat. After the money was received, they were released ashore. The kidnappers wanted ten thousand yuan for my mother and daughter. After being kidnapped, we spent two nights on a straw boat. On the fourth day, we were taken ashore and lived in a Jiangbei thatched shed for two days. Then we moved to a boat, rocking back and forth, without a fixed location. I don't know where. I was raped by three of them. My daughter is only sixteen years old, so she has suffered greatly from the bandits. (4) Female Hostage

Xu Yueqin Testified

She was sixteen years old, from Kunshan. On the ninth night of the fourth lunar month, I was kidnapped from my maternal grandmother's house. I was raped by a kidnapper who had a newly shaved head. I was violated three times in total. I am not yet betrothed to anyone. Because I had already gone to sleep with my mother that night, I don't know how many kidnappers there were. Because I was anxious, I can't remember. (5) Male Hostage

Wu Songqin Testified

He was forty-nine years old, from Qingpu, and lived in Nanxianjing Town. His occupation was farmer. The house I live in is quite big. Because the landlord moved out, he sold the house to me. I have many brothers and no place to live, so they first kidnapped them in my big house, and then they came to kidnap me. I stayed on the boat for one night. I moved to a firewood boat for two nights. Then, I lived on a Trapa natans boat for more than ten days. Then, I was taken ashore and lived in a Jiangbei thatched shed for one night. Then, I moved to a boat, rocking back and forth. I don't know where. Because my eyes were all blindfolded, I didn't know the direction. When I was kidnapped, there were about a dozen people. I was frightened when they kidnapped me. They used the butt of a gun to beat me in the waist. I also paid two thousand yuan to be ransomed. The night before yesterday, I tried to escape and ran to Dafu Temple in Dachang. I was chased and captured by the bandits. I shouted twice. The kidnappers then pressed me into the river to drink water so that I couldn't make a sound. I was still taken back to the pirate ship. After Judge Huang reviewed the testimony, he consulted with County Magistrate Qiu and ordered that the male hostage Wu Songqin, the female hostage Xu Wu Shi, and Xu Yueqin be handed over to the Guard Corps to escort them back to their hometowns. The kidnappers Tang Shaolian, Liu Aidao, and Yan Zhiqin were shackled and imprisoned for further investigation. The court was adjourned.

Good News from Kuling for Summer Retreat

Among the summer retreats in the Yangtze River basin of our country, Kuling is the best. It is not only high and cool, but also the vastness and magnificence of Mount Lu, the sound of springs everywhere, making it a great place for sightseeing and living. Therefore, every summer and autumn, Chinese and foreigners often travel thousands of miles with their families to live in the mountains. Even those who have long admired the famous mountains and take a few days off to enjoy the coolness of the mountains are also numerous. Last year, because the bandits in Jiangxi were not yet pacified, there were fewer tourists. In fact, Kuling is a famous summer resort, and the local authorities pay special attention to local security. The guards are usually very thorough. Moreover, the area is hundreds of miles wide, with overlapping mountains and dangerous stone paths, making it easy to defend, like a fortress. Therefore, the news of unrest in the mountains below was frequent, but the mountains were always peaceful. Everything was fine. Recently, according to friends in Xunyang, northern Jiangxi has been peaceful for a long time, and the large army is gathering in southern Jiangxi. The central government is focusing all its efforts on suppressing bandits. The tranquility of the mountains can be further guaranteed. Therefore, more and more Chinese and foreigners have been going to Kuling with their families. It is expected that the mountains this summer will be as prosperous as in previous years. Transportation to the mountains is also more convenient than in the past. China Travel Service has branches or reception centers in Jiujiang Riverbank, Lianhua Cave halfway up the mountain, and Kuling to take care of travelers and provide accommodation for temporary stays. Those who go to the mountains can entrust the agency to transport their luggage to the mountain after arriving in Xunyang by boat, and entrust them to hire cars and sedan chairs. The hotels in Kuling can also be booked in advance. Therefore, even those who have never been to Jiangxi can travel alone. After arriving in Xunyang, they can entrust the agency to take care of them. Recently, gasoline prices have soared, and the price of cars to the mountains has also increased. The fare from Jiujiang to Lianhua Cave is one yuan and eight jiao per passenger. Each car must carry four passengers. If you want to ride alone with one or two people, you must pay the fare for three people before the car will start. Currently, cars are not allowed from Lianhua Cave to Kuling. If you are afraid of walking, you can take a shoulder chair. Each chair bearer costs six jiao, usually four people.

The Local Court Specifies Office Hours for the Summer

The summer has arrived. According to custom, the Shanghai Local Court will only be open in the morning and closed in the afternoon. It has now been decided that from July 1st to the end of August, the office hours will be from 8 AM to 12 PM. However, in case of emergency matters, officers may be assigned to work on duty to handle them, so as to avoid dereliction of duty.

Children's Health Movement

Held Yesterday in Yangshupu, Pudong, Shanghai

Yesterday (the 23rd) was the first day of the Children's Health Movement held by the China Child Welfare Association in Yangshupu, Pudong, Shanghai. The 22nd was the preparation day, and a lantern parade was held in the evening. The participants were very enthusiastic. The situation of the past two days is summarized as follows.

Official Opening

At 6 PM on the 22nd, the opening ceremony was held. In the center of the stage hung a portrait and last will of the Prime Minister Sun Yat-Sen, and the Blue Sky White Sun flag. Next to it was a couplet that read, "Educate good children to serve society; promote healthy bodies to bring glory to the country," which was quite spectacular. The ceremony was presided over by Mr. Wang Guan, and Dr. Niu Huisheng, chaired the meeting and delivered the opening remarks. Mr. Wu Weide, Secretary-General, reported on the general overview of the Child Welfare Association's work. Then, Mr. Hu Hongquan, Director of the Municipal Health Bureau, Mr. Duck, Deputy Director of the Health Department of the Public Works Department, and Dr. E. F. Duck, President of the Pudong Public Association, gave speeches, which were mainly about promoting children's health, hoping that the public would pay attention to disease prevention, and avoid the criticism of digging a well when thirsty. There were more than 2,000 people in the audience.

Lantern Parade

After the opening ceremony, a large lantern parade was held. The participants were male and female students from the Child Welfare Education Center, Pudong Public Association, Yangshupu Primary School, Yangzheng Primary School, Children's Welfare Factory, and Decheng Primary School, about 1,000 people. Leading the procession were dozens of specially made fly lamps, mosquito lamps, egg lice mosquito lamps, which attracted the attention of passersby. The Public Works Department Police Department specially sent several capable policemen to protect the team, and the order was exceptionally well maintained. The team marched south on Meizhou Road, turned west to Taopeng Road, turned north into Pingliang Road, then circled Yangshupu and disbanded at the original location.

Film Screening

After returning from the parade, a hygiene film was shown outdoors behind the Pudong Public Association. About 5,000 people came to watch, shoulder to shoulder, and there was no space to move. The platform, fence, window frames, and tree branches were all covered with shadows. It can be said to be a grand occasion. After the film was shown, Ms. Xu Yunru directed the students of the Child Welfare Education Center to perform a hygiene drama, which was praised by the audience.

Physical Examination

From 9 AM on the 23rd, a children's health competition was held. Dr. Yang Suzhen, Ms. Chen Demei, Ms. Hua Meijie, and others examined the children's bodies. All children who joined the competition received several souvenirs from the Palm Olive Soap Company and other stores, and they left happily. There were seventy-five children participating in the competition.

Smallpox Vaccination

The Public Works Department Health Department, believing that children are most prone to diseases in the summer, specially sent seven doctors to the venue to provide free smallpox vaccinations for children. The vaccination started at 9 AM and ended at 12 PM. The work was very busy. A total of two hundred and forty-five children were vaccinated.

Free Injections

From 9 AM to 4 PM, the Public Works Department Health Department and the Municipal Health Bureau sent several representatives to administer vaccinations for adults and children inside and outside the venue. One hundred and sixty-seven children and five hundred and eighty-eight adults were vaccinated, totaling seven hundred and fifty-five people.

Children's Bathing

From 2 PM, Mrs. Wang Guan, Ms. Wang Aitian, Ms. Hua Aijie, and others presided over the free bathing for children. Most of those who signed up were children of workers, and they rushed to be first. A total of fifty-four children were bathed for free.

Meeting Performance

The meeting began at 8 PM. Mr. Hu Hongji, Director of the Municipal Health Bureau, sent a representative to give a lecture on the main points of children's health. Mr. Liu Zhanen, President of Shanghai University, Mr. Duck, Deputy Director of the Public Works Department Health Department, Mr. Chen Zhengfan, editor of the Child Welfare Monthly, and Dr. Lu Zhaien also came to visit and contribute. After the lecture, the Shanghai Youth Propaganda Team performed a children's drama, "The Play is Called 'Down with the Enemies of Children'," and a children's hygiene film was shown. More people came to watch than on the preparation day. The number of people was over 10,000. The meeting ended at 11:30 PM.

Wei Shan De Er Paris Sued

Citizens Accuse Zhonghe of Aiding and Abetting Theft

Shi Zhifu, manager of the Guomin Pharmacy at No. 410, Rue de Consulat, French Concession, filed a complaint in the Special District Court, accusing Xue Lianfu, manager of the Zhonghe Pharmacy at No. 32 1/2, Maugham Road, of aiding and abetting theft and other crimes. Yesterday, Judge Cheng Shangfeng heard the case in the Criminal Division II. Mr. Jin Zhiyuan, assistant, appeared in court on behalf of the plaintiff and testified that the Guomin Pharmacy was the sole distributor of Wei Shan De Er Paris. The retail price on the market was sixteen yuan and eight jiao per dozen. Recently, the same product was found to be fifteen yuan per dozen, resulting in a loss of business. After investigation, it was discovered that Luo Baohua and Yin Tingsheng, who had left the partnership, stole the goods and sold them to Zhonghe, so the price was so cheap. Therefore, I pretended to be a buyer from the Suzhou Zhongxi Pharmacy and went to Zhonghe to buy the goods. I bought one dozen for fifteen yuan. I wanted to buy more, and they said they would have more tomorrow. So I asked to buy two more dozen. Immediately, I heard them call 11217. This phone number was installed at the Guomin Pharmacy. I heard them talking to Luo Baohua, saying that the money had been given to your brother, and that kind of thing was needed for another twenty-four boxes. According to this tone, it can be known that they knew it was stolen goods, but they repeatedly bought them. There is actually a crime of aiding and abetting theft. Xue testified that he did buy Wei Shan De Er Paris, but he did not know that it was stolen. Because Luo claimed to be the manager of the Guomin Pharmacy, he could reduce the price. Besides, he only bought it once, a total of fifty-two bottles. Later, because he wanted two more dozen, he called Luo again. At that time, he really didn't know that Luo had stolen it. Moreover, he had no relationship with Luo, except that they were both students at Wuzhou Pharmacy in the past, so they knew each other. After reviewing the testimony, Judge Cheng announced that the hearing would be adjourned for one week for further hearing.

City Party Department Staff Reports

Yesterday morning at 11 AM, A Tu, a Shanghai gangster from Minhang who specializes in selling opium, bought a large amount of opium, 650 taels, from a Gu surnamed person in the concession. It was divided into large and small packages, marked with money. It was hidden in a charcoal basket, intending to be transported to the countryside for sale by the Shanghai-Minhang train. Unexpectedly, his plan was not secret. He was detected by a small rogue, who tailed him from behind. Near Lin Yin Road outside the West Gate, two rogues carried out a forced robbery. However, A Tu was not weak either, and he tried to reason with them, trying to redeem the items with money. A staff member of the City Party Department noticed this and called the police to come. A Tu and the opium were sent to the Second District Headquarters and then transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for legal action.
