Special Report

Second Report of Fei Tang (7th Continuation)

Abstract Translation of the Fourth and Fifth Sections

(A) Foreign Directors: Regarding practical suggestions for the future election of foreign directors, the reasons are summarized as follows: (1) The regulations for increasing the number of foreign directors should not only increase the number of foreign directors selected under the current system. (2) Regarding the representation of nationalities, a regulation should be established that is more practical than what can be represented under the current system. (3) A regulation should not be established for the sake of this national representation, which would cause the general electorate to be divided by nationality. (4) Both commerce and industry should have some direct representatives. (5) The separate regulations for direct representatives of commerce and industry will broaden the scope of choice for the general electorate in electing directors. (6) Members of chambers of commerce and members of other national organizations, some of whom lack the necessary qualifications to vote, have a close relationship with the interests of the International Settlement. (7) The plan suggested here will run parallel to the suggestions regarding the issue of Chinese directors and will not conflict. (B) Chinese Directors: Any plan to allow Chinese voters to elect their directors publicly, all the detailed measures in it, must be carefully considered. In the near future, the adoption of this plan may not be permitted by the situation. As far as I have explored, there may be significant difficulties in urging the most outstanding Chinese candidates to come forward and compete in public elections. However, it has been suggested to me that if it is stipulated that all candidates be nominated by groups composed of a majority of voters, or recommended by existing groups with considerable reputation in the International Settlement, then this difficulty can be overcome in part. The above has already suggested that any plan to allow Chinese directors to be directly elected by the general electorate should be supplemented by a plan, that is, some of the Chinese directors should still be elected in the same way as the current system, based on the direct full cooperation of Chinese groups, so that the elected people all have the proper qualifications to represent Chinese commercial and industrial interests. 5. Election Law: Adopt a suitable election law for public elections, including the usual safeguards to prevent fraud and undue pressure, and stipulate that all elections, except those handled by special groups authorized to choose their representatives, are supervised by officials of the Public Works Department. These elections are all conducted by voting. 6. Term of Directors: The term of directors in the future should be two years, with half of them re-elected every year. 7. Election Period: The annual election should always be held after the ratepayers' meeting. 8. Committee: Establish a regulation that allows the board of directors to elect temporary supplementary members of the committee, so as to determine the status of the committee member, and enable it to grant a certain range of executive power to each committee including temporary supplementary members. The chairman of the committee, if he is a temporary supplementary member, may attend the board of directors for the special purpose of submitting the committee's report. He has the right to speak when the recommendations contained in the report are debated, but cannot vote. 9. Appointment of Senior Officials: A committee should be organized whose specific function is to make recommendations to the board of directors on issues such as the appointment, reappointment, or dismissal of the heads of various departments and other senior officials within the Public Works Department. The board of directors shall not make any decisions on such appointments, reappointments, or dismissals unless specifically reported by the committee, and no new appointments of senior officials shall be made except in accordance with the committee's recommendations. The organization of the committee should have an agreed-upon basis so that it can represent residents of various nationalities. 10. Finance and Auditing: There should be a special regulation regarding the tasks of the Finance Committee to ensure that important financial matters are first studied and reported by the committee before being submitted to the board of directors for decision. The duties of the auditor must also be stipulated, and the nature of the report that must be prepared when certifying the annual income and expenditure accounts must be disclosed. 11. Publication: (A) Reform the content of the Public Works Department Gazette to make it more detailed about the various work situations in the bureau, and the text is more readable. The reasons why the Public Works Department adopted certain special measures are also explained in more detail. (B) Establish a more complete regulation so that newspapers can obtain timely information on issues related to the administration of the International Settlement. (C) When the proposed bylaws reach the final procedure, the board of directors should hold open meetings to perform its special legislative functions, so that the general public can fully understand the reasons for deciding to establish new bylaws. The open meeting of the board of directors held to achieve this purpose will replace the open discussion on the formulation of new bylaws, which has been given to special meetings of taxpayers. The report then added an opinion, saying that this reform involves an important limitation of the principle of joint and several liability, and said that the immediate implementation of the various recommendations may not be permitted by the situation. 12. Chinese and English Names of the International Settlement and the Public Works Department: The International Settlement itself and its主管機關 (Zhugejiguan - Chief Authority) Public Works Department should adopt Chinese and English names that express the broadest international nature of all its "public" words.

Chapter Seven

Describes the issues left for further consideration in Chapter Six, that is, since Chinese directors are a minority in the Public Works Department, whether special regulations are needed to protect the interests of the Chinese. It then clarifies the main issues that distinguish the interests of the Chinese from the interests of other residents, such as the issue of educational facilities for the Chinese. Regarding medical services, hospital facilities, and the convenience of sports, the interests of the Chinese must also be roughly considered separately. Whether there should be sufficient regulations for the above expenditures is a question. Before considering this question, the report first considers how Chinese directors have participated in board meetings since they first took office in 1928. Since the first implementation of the Chinese representative system in April 1928, there has been a sign of the relationship between Chinese directors and their foreign colleagues, that is, both sides are willing to make full use of all new opportunities in the conference seats to discuss and cooperate. If the attendance of directors is not important, it has no impact on the general trend of the Public Works Department's policy. This is completely wrong, because the power of Chinese directors should not only be viewed in terms of their number. Since Chinese directors first took office in 1928, the Public Works Department has indeed shown a clear development and adopted a new trend in the policy of several important events. The report then raises three issues, the substantive progress of which is indeed a direct result of the attendance of Chinese directors. What are these three issues? (1) The progress of education policy, (2) The new policy of employing Chinese to fill senior positions included in the recommendations of the Salary Committee, (3) The publication of the Public Works Department Gazette and Annual Report in Chinese. The power of Chinese directors regarding the decision to ban dog racing in the International Settlement and other events was also mentioned. The new education policy of the Public Works Department is detailed in the report of the Education Committee published in December 1930, and its principles have been accepted by the Board of Directors, which has been summarized. The economic aspects of this policy have also been considered. The report points out that the Chinese representatives' advocacy of increasing educational facilities and other actions inevitably involves increasing taxes, and in the past, the Chinese have expressed their keen feelings about the proposal to increase taxes. An important lesson is that Chinese voters and taxpayers and voters and taxpayers of other nationalities must understand that the public undertakings of improvement and the new institutions that benefit the people must be funded by increased taxes. Furthermore, if you want to consider whether this price is worth paying, the benefits that must be taken into account are not the interests of individuals, but the general interests of all residents. The funds needed to implement the new education policy should be subsidized by all residents. The fair distribution of these funds to various parts of the residents should be based on the comparison of the needs of each part, rather than the number of wheels that each part has transferred. This will reverse the previous situation. Although the taxes paid by the Chinese accounted for more than half of the income of the Public Works Department, the fees for educational facilities obtained by the Chinese only accounted for a small part of the allocated educational expenses. In the future, if we insist on the new education policy and implement the new education plan, the number of all educational expenses that must be allocated to Chinese schools will exceed the proportion of Chinese wheels in municipal income. The report then makes a suggestion that "If the representatives of Chinese society are willing, a guarantee can be included in the property charter, stipulating that unless the majority of Chinese directors agree to reduce the specified number within any special year, in any case, for at least a certain period of time, the education and other specific expenses of the International Settlement for the special interests of the Chinese people in the boundary shall be increased by a few percent each year. There is also a possible alternative method, that is, within the property charter, stipulate a special annual land tax and house rent, and determine its percentage according to Article 9 of the property charter, for education and social improvement, and it can be stipulated that a fixed part of the income from this tax should be used for the special interests of the Chinese. The report suggests that there must be a regulation for the schools established by the Public Works Department and the schools subsidized by the Public Works Department, so that the interests of all parts of the International Settlement can have reasonable and necessary guarantees. What is this regulation? That is, any method of managing schools established by the Public Works Department and any plan to subsidize private schools must be accompanied by a condition, that is, "The education of each related school shall not have the slightest purpose of encouraging international or racial antipathy." In terms of the nature of textbooks adopted by some schools, this condition is not considered superfluous, because the governance system of the International Settlement is based on international partnership, not only the partnership between foreign countries, but also the partnership between China and various foreign countries. Assuming that the Public Works Department, composed of representatives of various nationalities, cooperates for the common interests of all citizens to handle the administration of the International Settlement, it knowingly or intentionally allocates any part of its income to maintain various schools, and the children of various nationalities represented by the education community are convinced that, historically, it is necessary to treat each other as hereditary enemies, or that hating foreigners is the first duty of a good citizen of a country. Is it not strange? The international cooperation of the Public Works Department cannot be based on the international hatred of various schools. The regulations proposed above apply quite broadly, meaning that propaganda against any one country or any number of countries should also be prohibited. There is no doubt that it is difficult to guarantee that this regulation can be observed unswervingly, but if this regulation can be recognized by the public, it is already a guarantee and an important step towards the right path in the way of heaven.

Chapter Eight

Describes the three topics specifically mentioned in the third question, that is, the various shortcomings of the current situation, as well as the reforms that should be made regarding (B) the powers and tasks of the Public Works Department in the International Settlement, (C) the powers that consuls and ministers of various countries can exercise over the International Settlement affairs, and (D) the relationship between the Public Works Department and the Chinese government authorities. The current situation of the above events has been considered. Regarding the power of the Public Works Department and the relationship between the Public Works Department and the Chinese authorities, the discussion is as follows: The fundamental difference in nature between the power exercised by the Public Works Department and the power exercised by the Chinese government officials has been explained in the first parts of this report. Although the new governance system of Chinese municipal areas is very different from the old governance system under the Taoist and his subordinates, and represents great progress, there is still a significant difference in principle between the Public Works Department's governance system and the Chinese-ruled municipal government, because on the one hand, it is still an organ whose power is generally of an unlimited nature, and the laws and regulations on which it is based allow individual officials to enter and exit at will. The scope is also wide, and the exercise of this power by this organ is not controlled by independent courts. As for the other hand, it is another organ whose power is much more limited, and the regulations on which it is based allow individual officials to enter and exit at will. The space is very narrow, and it must be controlled by a completely independent court. All the objections to the two organs exercising mutually independent powers in the same area for the same people still exist today. Assuming that the government of the International Settlement is still well-governed by the Public Works Department's governance system, the powers exercised by the Public Works Department in the International Settlement must still be of a unique nature and cannot create a system that forcibly combines the governance work of the two organs in the same area. This means that the power to govern the International Settlement cannot be divided, so that part of it is exercised by the officials of the International Settlement and part of it is exercised by the officials of the municipal government in the Chinese area, and the work of the two groups of officials is not related to each other. Methods of cooperation can be agreed upon and should be agreed upon, but only within the scope of the Public Works Department's consent and under the conditions of its consent can Chinese municipal officials exercise their powers in the International Settlement. The issue of applying the laws implemented by bureaucratic authorities in the Chinese area to the International Settlement has been discussed. The difficulties of the Public Works Department assuming the general responsibility for implementing this law in the International Settlement have been revealed. The issue of cooperation between the Public Works Department and the Chinese authorities has been discussed again as follows: From the surface, since a new-style municipal government has been established in the Chinese area linked to the International Settlement, it can be hoped that it can improve the relationship between the Public Works Department and the local Chinese authorities. For hygiene and police affairs, both parties have been prepared to recognize their common interests and can adopt various methods within their respective jurisdictions to provide valuable assistance to each other. However, although there has been some cooperation between the two organs, this cooperation has not been smooth in certain aspects and has sometimes resulted in many conflicts. If it was clearly stated at the beginning that the International Settlement is still an independent area and is not under the jurisdiction of the Chinese municipal government, then there could have been better expectations for the cooperation between the two organs and the progress of friendly relations. However, the request put forward by the representatives of the Chinese municipal government was that all the slightly vague regulations in the Shanghai Special Municipal Organization Law have the effect of including the International Settlement within the Chinese municipal area. This request has had unfortunate consequences. Some enthusiastic officials in the Chinese area regard it as their duty to take independent actions within the International Settlement and disregard the powers of the Public Works Department, especially in matters that the Public Works Department has not been clearly authorized to handle. The Public Works Department and its officials had to resist this attempt. Although there were political difficulties and conflicts over important issues of jurisdiction, there has been valuable cooperation between the two parties for certain common purposes. They have responded to and worked together to defend against public dangers such as public disturbances, epidemics, and food shortages. However, a better environment should be created to obtain closer cooperation. If a clear agreement can be reached on the jurisdictional issues in dispute, it will greatly benefit the creation of this environment. The addition of Chinese to the Board of Directors and other changes to the Organizational Law, as suggested in this report, are intended to allow the Chinese community to fully participate in the administration of the International Settlement, which should contribute to improvements. It is strongly advocated that the cooperation between the Public Works Department, the unified legal organ of the International Settlement, and the Chinese authorities outside the settlement should be in harmony with the cooperation between Chinese and foreign residents in the International Settlement. Under the new circumstances, the Public Works Department should no longer be regarded as a foreign organ, and all its actions should be guarded against, monitored, and restricted as much as possible, but should be regarded as an organ in which Chinese and foreign residents work together to manage the interests of the residents of the parts of the International Settlement that cannot be separated from all Shanghai residents. Is this claim not fair? If this can be done, it should enable the directors and their powers of the Public Works Department of the International Settlement on the one hand, and the officials of the municipal government in the Chinese area connected to the International Settlement on the other hand, to regard each other as allies and colleagues, rather than as rivals or enemies.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday said that it is cloudy here, and there is a cyclone on the Shandong coast, caused by a small low pressure passing through northern Jiangsu and moving towards the northeast-east. There is a strong northwesterly wind in the Bohai Sea, and the wind in the East China Sea is uncertain. Also, the highest temperature in this port in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 84.9, the lowest was 70.0, the highest on the same day last year was 89.7, and the lowest was 69.9.
